                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Sandwich-Like Hierarchically Porous Carbon/Graphene Composite as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Yang; Yin, Ya-Xia; Guo, Yu-Guo; Wan, Li-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1301584/1-1301584/5</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This article proposes a strategy by designing a sandwich-like nanocomposite to overcome the disadvantages of the non-graphitized carbon materials.  This article summarizes that the developed a facile ionothermal method to synthesize sandwich-like hierarchically porous carbon/graphene composite, in which hierarchical porous carbon facilitates Na+ insertion and graphene guarantees the high electronic cond. for electrons supply.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrul7DVrUFn6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljLVGzQTc-z7A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpt1Wjurk%253D&amp;md5=3dec7b7bfc133e4038c2ad0de8f47e12</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7929"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y. W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L. Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sup>+</sup> Intercalation Pseudocapacitance in Graphene-Coupled Titanium Oxide Enabling Ultra-Fast Sodium Storage and Long-Term Cyclin</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6929</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms7929</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6929%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DC.%2BJ.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BW.%2BWen%26author%3DX.%2BL.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BL.%2BJi%26author%3DM.%2BY.%2BYan%26author%3DL.%2BQ.%2BMai%26author%3DP.%2BHu%26author%3DB.%2BShan%26author%3DY.%2BH.%2BHuang%26title%3DNa%252B%2BIntercalation%2BPseudocapacitance%2Bin%2BGraphene-Coupled%2BTitanium%2BOxide%2BEnabling%2BUltra-Fast%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Band%2BLong-Term%2BCyclin%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms7929&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b03541&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms7929&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6929</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGrV7K8Tq5mLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaD6UqiNjqRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2lurzK&amp;md5=99303fd99ef59044874690750282067a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H. B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span>. <i>Acc. Chem.                 10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D231-240%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DW.%2BLuo%26author%3DF.%2BShen%26author%3DC.%2BBommier%26author%3DH.%2BL.%2BZhu%26author%3DX.%2BL.%2BJi%26author%3DL.%2BB.%2BHu%26title%3DNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%253A%2BMaterials%2Band%2BElectrochemistry%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b03541&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaD6UqiNjqRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b15757"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C. Q.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt- and Cadmium-Based Metal-Organic Frameworks as High Performance Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries and Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt- and Cadmium-Based Metal-Organic Frameworks as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries and Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Caifu; Xu, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7160-7168</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two multifunctional metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) with the same coordination mode, [Co(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Co(L) MOF"] and [Cd(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Cd(L) MOF"] (L = 5-aminoisophthalic acid) have been fabricated via a simple and versatile scalable solvothermal approach at 85 °C for 24 h.  The relationship between the structure of the electrode materials (esp. the coordination water and different metal ions) and the electrochem. properties of MOFs have been investigated for the first time.  And then the possible electrochem. mechanisms of the electrodes have been studied and proposed.  In addn., MOFs/RGO hybrid materials were prepd. via ball milling, which demonstrated better electrochem. performances than those of individual Co(L) MOF and Cd(L) MOF.  For example, when Co(L) MOF/RGO was applied as anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), it retained 206 mA h g-1 after 330 cycles at 500 mA g-1 and 1185 mA h g-1 could be obtained after 50 cycles at 100 mA g-1 for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  The high-discharge capacity, excellent cyclic stability combined with the facile synthesis procedure enable Co(L) MOF- and Cd(L) MOF-based materials to be prospective anode materials for SIBs and LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrYWKsq_6KCqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgu3rlpl_IdTg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitFCntr4%253D&amp;md5=91879f6af546dcca6f04a7843c7d36f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700606"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion storage properties of nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/reduced graphene oxide composite powders prepared by a spray drying process and the nanoscale Kirkendall effect</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, G. D.; Cho, J. S.; Kang, Y. C.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">16781-16788</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Spray-drying and the nanoscale Kirkendall diffusion process are used to prep. nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composite powders with excellent Na-ion storage properties.  Metallic Ni nanopowder-decorated rGO powders, formed as intermediate products, are transformed into composite powders of nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/rGO with mixed crystal structures of Ni3S2 and Ni9S8 phases by the sulfidation process under H2S gas.  Nickel sulfide/rGO composite powders with the main crystal structure of Ni3S2 are also prepd. as comparison samples by the direct sulfidation of nickel acetate-graphene oxide (GO) composite powders obtained by spray-drying.  In electrochem. properties, the discharge capacities at the 150th cycle of the nickel sulfide/rGO composite powders prepd. by sulfidation of the Ni/rGO composite and nickel acetate/GO composite powders at a c.d. of 0.3 A g-1 are 449 and 363 mA h g-1, resp.; their capacity retentions, calcd. from the tenth cycle, are 100 and 87%.  The nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/rGO composite powders possess structural stability over repeated Na-ion insertion and extn. processes, and also show excellent rate performance for Na-ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCYAlXgf05mrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgu3rlpl_IdTg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVGnu7zF&amp;md5=a66f406af3c50fff793b6535f7fbd88d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.01.079"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox-active org. polymers are promising cathode electrodes owing to the advantages of open and flexible frame-works, renewability and environmental friendliness.  Sodium salt of poly(2, 5-dihydroxy-p-benzoquinonyl sulfide)/RGO (Na2PDHBQS/RGO) composite has been fabricated via a convenient route and applied as a high performance and stable cathode for sodium ion batteries.  The Na2PDHBQS/RGO was investigated in ether-based electrolyte, which demonstrated better electrochem. performances (228, 214, 203, 193, 172, and 147 mAh g-1 at 0.1, 0.2, 0.4, 0.8, 2 and 4C, resp.) than that in traditional ester-based ones.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supported Nanotube Arrays of Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Enabling Ultrastable and Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Fu, Shidong; Wu, Chao; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">28</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2259-2265</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxSp6BahJSMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42944J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb-C nanofibers with long cycle life as an anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Lin; Hu, Xiaohong; Qian, Jiangfeng; Pei, Feng; Wu, Fayuan; Mao, Rongjun; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxSp6BahJSMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgxSp6BahJSMA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhslCgsbnE&amp;md5=75362e7708fe6434655290ce0aa7cac0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b00179"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nickel Disulfide-Graphene Nanosheets Composites with Improved Electrochemical Performance for Sodium Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Tianshi; Hu, Pu; Zhang, Chuanjian; Du, Huiping; Zhang, Zhonghua; Wang, Xiaogang; Chen, Shougang; Xiong, Junwei; Cui, Guanglei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel disulfide-graphene nanosheets (NiS2-GNS) composites were successfully synthesized via a simple and mild hydrothermal method.  It was revealed by SEM and transmission electron microscopy images that the spherical NiS2 nanoparticles with a diam. of 200-300 nm were uniformly dispersed on graphene nanosheets.  Na+ electrochem. storage properties including cycling performance and high-rate capability of NiS2-GNS composites were investigated, demonstrating a superior reversible capacity of 407 mAh g-1 with the capacity retention of 77% over 200 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 C.  Furthermore, even at a large c.d. of 2 C, a high capacity of 168 mAh g-1 can still remain, which is much higher than that of pristine NiS2 materials.  The enhancement in electrochem. properties might be attributed to the synergetic effect endowed by high cond. of graphene and novel structure of the electrode material.  Combined with the advantages of low cost and environmental benignity, NiS2-GNS composite would be a potential anode material for sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoD92985WAQn7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-quAXUVplHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjs12itbY%253D&amp;md5=2fac39852cc960d5205f24b170d22d65</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.06.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Morphology-dependent performance of nanostructured Ni3S2/Ni anode electrodes for high performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Xiaosheng; Li, Xifei; Bai, Zhimin; Yan, Bo; Li, Dejun; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides have been treated as promising materials for lithium-ion battery, and recently more and more attention has been paid to its applications in sodium-ion batteries.  In our context, three Ni3S2 nanostructures directly grown on Ni foam were successfully designed using a facile hydrothermal method.  The influences of the morphol. on the performance evolution for sodium-ion batteries were studied in detail.  As a result, it was found that the initial drop, gradual increase, convex type decline and concave type decline in the performance evolutions were mainly controlled by Rct, Rsf, pulverization, and internal stress, resp.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural and chemical synergistic effect of CoS nanoparticles and porous carbon nanorods for high-performance sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Limin; Zhang, Kai; Sheng, Jinzhi; An, Qinyou; Tao, Zhanliang; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">35</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">281-289</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering inherent large structural deterioration of conversion-type anode materials during repeated sodiation/desodiation process, the ingenious integration of both nanostructure engineering and chem. hybridization is highly desirable and challenging.  Here, ultrafine CoS nanoparticles embedded in porous carbon nanorods (denoted as 7-CoS/C) were facilely fabricated via simultaneous in-situ carbonization and sulfidation of Co-metal org. frameworks (Co-MOF) and have been applied as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Benefiting from the advantageous embedding architecture between the nanoparticles and porous nanorods, the 7-CoS/C delivers long-term cycling stability (542 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles with a capacity retention of 91.4% at 1 A g-1) and excellent rate performance (discharge capacities of 510 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 and 356 mAh g-1 even at 40 A g-1), which is proved to be characterized of partial pseudocapacitive behaviors during the sodiation/desodiation process.  In addn., Na3V2(PO4)3/7-CoS/C full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 has been assembled and exhibits a capacity of 352 mAh g-1 at 0.5 A g-1.  This meaningful approach can be extended to build embedded porous structure of other hybrid composites for next-generation energy-storage technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9KtRozkoFx7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-quAXUVplHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlslejtbs%253D&amp;md5=6f81f0741eecaa1345bac17a099cb17f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201602933"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W. X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering Hierarchical Hollow Nickel Sulfide Spheres for High-Performance Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Funct.                 10.1002/adfm.201602933</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D26%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D7479-7485%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DD.%2BZhang%26author%3DW.%2BP.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BH.%2BDou%26author%3DY.%2BZ.%2BJiang%26author%3DS.%2BX.%2BDou%26title%3DEngineering%2BHierarchical%2BHollow%2BNickel%2BSulfide%2BSpheres%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201602933&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b03541&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201602933&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering Hierarchical Hollow Nickel Sulfide Spheres for High-Performance Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Dan; Sun, Wenping; Zhang, Yu; Dou, Yuhai; Jiang, Yinzhu; Dou, Shi Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7479-7485</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for energy storage due to the abundance of sodium, esp. for grid distribution systems.  The practical implementation of SIBs, however, is severely hindered by their low energy d. and poor cycling stability due to the poor electrochem. performance of the existing electrodes.  Here, to achieve high-capacity and durable sodium storage with good rate capability, hierarchical hollow NiS spheres with porous shells composed of nanoparticles are designed and synthesized by tuning the reaction parameters.  The formation mechanism of this unique structure is systematically investigated, which is clearly revealed to be Ostwald ripening mechanism on the basis of the time-dependent morphol. evolution.  The hierarchical hollow structure provides sufficient electrode/electrolyte contact, shortened Na+ diffusion pathways, and high strain-tolerance capability.  The hollow NiS spheres deliver high reversible capacity (683.8 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capability (337.4 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and good cycling stability (499.9 mAh g-1 with 73% retention after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqILcValYXCmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-quAXUVplHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVymtrbN&amp;md5=df1523f34e777d5f61481d30ef557f22</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.10.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T. K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Layered Nickel Sulfide-Reduced Graphene Oxide Composites Synthesized <i>via</i> Microwave-Assisted Method as High Performance Anode Materials of Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Layered nickel sulfide-reduced graphene oxide composites synthesized via microwave-assisted method as high performance anode materials of sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Qin, Wei; Chen, Taiqiang; Lu, Ting; Chua, Daniel H. C.; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">302</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">202-209</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered nickel sulfide (NS)-reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites are prepd. via a simple microwave-assisted method and subsequent annealing in N2/H2 atmosphere.  A detailed array of characterization tools are used to study their morphol., structure and electrochem. performance.  It was found that these composites exhibit significantly improved sodium-ion storage ability as compared with pure NS under galvanostatic cycling at a specific current of 100 mA g-1 in a potential limitation of 0.005-3.0 V.  Furthermore, the composite with the RGO content of 35 wt.% achieves a high max. reversible specific capacity of about 391.6 mA h g-1 at a specific current of 100 mA g-1 after 50 cycles.  These results prove that NS-RGO composites are highly promising when applied directly as anode materials in sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpb_pCc5C-0R7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOEX--a27lEg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslems7fL&amp;md5=7fd6ed7370ae6c13489238d135cd46d8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C4EE03759F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pyrite FeS<sub>2</sub> for High-Rate and Long-Life Rechargeable Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1309</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1316</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pyrite FeS2 for high-rate and long-life rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Cheng, Fangyi; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Chen, Chengcheng; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1309-1316</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.  This shows that the prodn. of rechargeable sodium batteries with FeS2 microspheres is viable for com. utilization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFxqeM-EGKh7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOEX--a27lEg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1arsL0%253D&amp;md5=25c3d019d88687effcc5109727ee9bce</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201500196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">FeSe<sub>2</sub> Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">FeSe2 Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Hu, Zhe; Liu, Xue; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use is demonstrated of FeSe2 as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1.  The conversion reaction of FeSe2 + 4Na+ + 4e ↔ Fe + 2Na2Se has been confirmed.  Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqNZQmIWuA02rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOEX--a27lEg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmslens7Y%253D&amp;md5=0ecc7e52e3b809d3dadbf828186e0859</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201701744"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interlaced NiS2-MoS2 nanoflake-nanowires as efficient hydrogen evolution electrocatalysts in basic solutions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">An, Tiance; Wang, Yang; Tang, Jing; Wei, Wei; Cui, Xiaoqi; Alenizi, Abdullah M.; Zhang, Lijuan; Zheng, Gengfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13439-13443</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrocatalytic activity of transition metal sulfides is strongly correlated with the active edge sites and cond. of the catalysts.  Here we developed a hybrid nanowire structure consisting of NiS2-MoS2 interlaced nanoflakes by the thermal conversion of nickel molybdate (NiMoO4) nanowire precursors.  The obtained NiS2-MoS2 interlaced nanoflakes have sub-200 nm sizes with abundant active edge sites and defects, as well as synergistic nanoscale interfaces between NiS2 and MoS2 throughout the whole structure.  The hetero-nanowires exhibit superior hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) catalytic activity including a low onset potential of 76 mV and a small Tafel slope of 70 mV dec-1 in a 1 M KOH aq. soln., which substantially exceeds those of most of the metal sulfide HER catalysts including individual NiS2 and MoS2 nanostructures in basic solns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBzNHqSQIEFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljOEX--a27lEg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1WmtbfE&amp;md5=8222f389eb32031ad1089919c0d77a96</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1007/s10008-017-3600-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of NiS/carbon composites as anodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jinkai; Cao, Daxian; Yang, Guidong; Yang, Yaodong; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Electrochemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">21</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3047-3055</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JSSEFS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1432-8488</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We demonstrate a general solid-state synthesis of nickel sulfide (NiS) and carbon-based composites (NiS/C) via simple thermal decompn. of nickel dibutyldithiocarbamate (C18H36N2NiS4) under ambient atm., which can be applied to various carbon-based materials such as 2D graphene nanosheets (GNSs), 1D carbon nanotubes (CNTs), and 0D carbon black (CB).  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the as-prepd. NiS/C composites demonstrate excellent sodium storage properties including superior cycle stability and rate capability, delivering reversible capacities of 483 (for NiS/GNSs), 394 (for NiS/CNTs), and 413 mAh/g (for NiS/CB) at a c.d. of 200 mA/g after 100 cycles, resp., which are much higher than that of the bare NiS counterpart (136 mAh/g at 200 mA/g after 100 cycles).  Moreover, reversible capacities of 372 mAh/g for NiS/GNSs, 331 mAh/g for NiS/CNTs, and 317 mAh/g for NiS/CB are realized at a high rate of 2 A/g.  The excellent electrochem. performance can be attributed to the introduction of the carbon-based materials, which not only serve as efficient buffering matrixes to tolerate the vol. changes of NiS upon sodiation/desodiation but also improve the electrode cond.  More importantly, this work provides a straightforward and general synthetic approach for designing various NiS/C composites as high-performance anodes for electrochem. energy storage.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reduced Graphene Oxide-Induced Recrystallization of NiS Nanorods to Nanosheets and the Improved Na-Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Qin; Xie, Jian; Zhu, Tiejun; Cao, Gaoshao; Zhao, Xinbing; Zhang, Shichao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3511-3518</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prepn. of two-dimensional (2D) graphene-like materials is currently an emerging field in materials science since the discovery of single-atom-thick graphene prepd. by mech. cleavage.  In this work, we proposed a new method to prep. 2D NiS, where reduced graphene oxide (rGO) was found to induce the recrystn. of NiS from nanorods to nanosheets in a hydrothermal process.  The process and mechanism of recrystn. have been clarified by various characterization techniques, including SEM, transmission electron microscopy (TEM), energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) mapping, and XPS.  The characterization of ex situ NiS/rGO products by SEM and EDS mapping indicates that the recrystn. of NiS from nanorods to nanosheets is realized actually through an exfoliation process, while the characterization of in situ NiS/rGO products by SEM, TEM, and EDS mapping reveals the exfoliation process.  The XPS result demonstrates that hydrothermally assisted chem. bonding occurs between NiS and rGO, which induces the exfoliation of NiS nanorods into nanosheets.  The obtained NiS/rGO composite shows promising Na-storage properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqY5KHERzDl-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljga8jT9GjWog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXksF2rtb0%253D&amp;md5=e7ec208b87afc61d8e4703751d36bc98</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acscatal.5b00154"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ganesan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanetuntikul, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shanmugam, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt Sulfide Nanoparticles Grown on Nitrogen and Sulfur Codoped Graphene Oxide: An Efficient Electrocatalyst for Oxygen Reduction and Evolution Reactions</span>. <i>ACS Catal.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3625</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3637</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cobalt Sulfide Nanoparticles Grown on Nitrogen and Sulfur Codoped Graphene Oxide: An Efficient Electrocatalyst for Oxygen Reduction and Evolution Reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ganesan, Pandian; Prabu, Moni; Sanetuntikul, Jakkid; Shanmugam, Sangaraju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Catalysis</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3625-3637</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACCACS</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. oxygen evolution and redn. reactions have received great attention due to their importance in several key technologies such as fuel cells, electrolyzers, and metal-air batteries.  Here, we present a simple approach to the prepn. of cobalt sulfide nanoparticles in situ grown on a nitrogen- and sulfur-codoped graphene oxide surface.  The particle size and phase were controlled by changing the treatment temp.  Cobalt sulfide nanoparticles dispersed on graphene oxide hybrids were successfully prepd. by a solid-state thermolysis approach at different temps. (400, 500, and 600°) using cobalt-thiourea complex and graphene oxide.  X-ray diffraction studies revealed that hybrids prepd. at 400 and 500 °C result in pure CoS2 phase, whereas the hybrid prepd. at 600 °C exhibits Co9S8 phase.  XPS studies revealed that nitrogen and sulfur simultaneously codoped on the graphene oxide surface, and these sites act to anchor the CoS2 nanoparticles strongly on the GO surface.  The strong coupling between CoS2 and N,S-GO was reflected in the improvement of the oxygen electrode potential.  CoS2(400)/N,S-GO showed an outstanding oxygen electrode activity with a potential of about 0.82 V against a reversible hydrogen electrode in alk. medium, which is far better than the performance of precious catalysts such as Pt/C (1.16 V), Ru/C (1.01 V), and Ir/C (0.92 V).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1sLK9FiN1f7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljga8jT9GjWog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFOgtbY%253D&amp;md5=ef218509d1975cd741dfe4878d7c84cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.04.011"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrafine Co1-xS nanoparticles embedded in a nitrogen-doped porous carbon hollow nanosphere composite as an anode for superb sodium-ion batteries and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Caifu; Guo, Lijun; He, Yanyan; Shang, Limei; Qian, Yitai; Xu, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2804-2811</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cobalt sulfides are attractive as intriguing candidates for anodes in SIBs and LIBs owing to their unique chem. and phys. properties.  In this study, a precursor of Co1-xS with a uniform and hollow nanospherical architecture is obtained with a high yield via a mild solvothermal method in the presence of 2-methylimidazole at first.  Then, Co1-xS, Co1-xS/C (ultrafine Co1-xS nanoparticles embedded in the shells of the nitrogen-doped porous carbon hollow nanosphere), and Co1-xS@C (Co1-xS nanoparticles entirely covered by an external amorphous carbon layer) were selectively fabricated via direct calcination or PPy coating &amp; calcination of the obtained precursor.  Co1-xS/C shows best electrochem. performance than the other two materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Besides the excellent rate performance, a high reversible discharge capacity of 320 mA g-1 can be retained after 130 cycles at 1 A g-1.  The impressive performance may be attributed to the unique structure, higher cond., and more active sites of Co1-xS/C.  In addn., 559 mA h g-1 was maintained after 100 cycles at 500 mA g-1 when the Co1-xS/C composite was applied as an anode in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  The high reversible capacity, excellent cycle stability combined with the facile synthesis procedure render Co1-xS/C a prospective anode material for rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq6CFZ4oCsNr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljga8jT9GjWog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXjs1Krtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=065e3489d530103302115fa2699799bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b06625"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Three-Dimensional Graphene Encapsulated with Hollow FeP@Carbon Nanocomposite as Outstanding Anode Material for Lithium Ion and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiujuan; Chen, Kai; Wang, Gang; Liu, Xiaojie; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11602-11616</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have been extensively investigated owing to their high theor. capacities and relatively low intercalation potentials vs Li/Li+, but their practical applications have been hindered by low elec. cond. and dramatic vol. variation during cycling.  In this work, an interesting strategy for the rational design of graphene (GR) encapsulated with a hollow FeP@carbon nanocomposite (H-FeP@C@GR) via a combination of a hydrothermal route, a carbon-coating process, phosphidation treatment, and carbothermic reaction is reported.  The hollow FeP (H-FeP) nanospheres shelled with thin carbon layers are wonderfully incorporated into the GR matrix, interconnecting to form a three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical architecture.  Such a design offers distinct advantages for FeP-based anode materials for both lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, the 3D omnibearing conductive networks from the GR skeleton and outer coating carbon can provide an open freeway for electron/ion transport, promoting the electrode reaction kinetics.  In addn., the wrapping of an H-FeP nanosphere in a thin carbon layer enables the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on the carbon layer surface instead of on the individual H-FeP surface, preventing the continual re-forming of the SEI.  When used as anode materials for LIBs and SIBs, H-FeP@C@GR exhibited excellent electrochem. performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJNbfRlD70dbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljga8jT9GjWog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhsbnP&amp;md5=60e49fafbda32645938e58b743ba2e5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00201G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A binary metal organic framework derived hierarchical hollow Ni3S2/Co9S8/N-doped carbon composite with superior sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xinye; Zou, Feng; Liu, Kewei; Qiang, Zhe; Taubert, Clinton J.; Ustriyana, Putu; Vogt, Bryan D.; Zhu, Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A binary Ni/Co metal org. framework (Ni-Co-MOF) with a hollow-sphere structure that is decorated with cone-shaped protrusions was prepd. via a facile solvothermal reaction.  Carbonization and sulfurization of the Ni-Co-MOF produced a Ni3S2/Co9S8/N-doped C composite that retained the hierarchical structure.  The final composite material presents exceptional electrochem. performance when used as an anode in Na-ion batteries.  A reversible specific capacity of 419.9 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.1 A/g was achieved after 100 cycles, with an exceptional capacity retention of 98.6%.  Superior rate capability was also demonstrated: an av. capacity of 323.2 mAh/g at a c.d. of 2 A/g can be achieved.  This exceptional performance can be attributed to the unique nano-architecture derived from the MOF precursor, as the resultant material possesses an ideal profile for an excellent anode material: ultrafine Ni3S2 and Co9S8 particles (∼7 nm), a hollow, porous structure, and an ultrathin N-doped C coating.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGphf2SkKOhqv7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljga8jT9GjWog"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjvFajsrc%253D&amp;md5=4f1e03f96d42d268122c8a9877459686</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA00557E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Design of pomegranate-like clusters with NiS2 nanoparticles anchored on nitrogen-doped porous carbon for improved sodium ion storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Jiabao; Li, Jinliang; Yan, Dong; Hou, Shujin; Xu, Xingtao; Lu, Ting; Yao, Yefeng; Mai, Wenjie; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6595-6605</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel sulfide, a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), has drawn a lot of attention due to its natural abundance, low cost, rich types and high theor. specific capacity (Ni3S2: 446, NiS: 591 and NiS2: 879 mA h g-1).  However, the huge vol. change-induced severe electrode pulverization results in the low specific capacity and poor cycling stability of nickel sulfide electrodes.  Herein, in this paper, we developed a metal-org. framework (MOF) strategy to prep. pomegranate-like clusters with small NiS2 nanoparticles anchored on nitrogen doped porous graphitic carbon networks (NiS2/NC) via successive carbonization and sulfidation.  When evaluated as an anode for SIBs, the as-prepd. NiS2/NC hybrid exhibited a high reversible capacity of 505.7 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, excellent rate capability (294.4 mA h g-1 at 3 A g-1) and robust cycling stability with a capacity of 356.2 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, which outperforms most of the nickel sulfide based electrodes reported so far.  The excellent cycling performance and rate capability for SIBs can be attributed to the unique structure inherited from nickel based MOFs, in situ fabrication strategy, high capacity of NiS2, and conductive and buffering features of the nitrogen-doped graphitic carbon networks, demonstrating the great potential of the as-prepd. NiS2/NC hybrid for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqyF8tMrvq_a7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhG27qwr3XXJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXksFagsLc%253D&amp;md5=b1af16a601c2a22cf423f7a9c4691f0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D hierarchical defect-rich NiMo3S4 nanosheet arrays grown on carbon textiles for high-performance sodium-ion batteries and hydrogen evolution reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Dezhi; Wang, Ye; Lim, Yew Von; Huang, Shaozhuan; Zhang, Jun; Liu, Bo; Chen, Tupei; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">460-470</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A hierarchical hybrid nanostructure composed of NiMo3S4 nanosheet arrays with abundant exposed edges on flexible carbon textiles (denoted as NiMo3S4/CTs) has been designed and synthesized for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and electrocatalytic hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  The novel NiMo3S4 nanostructure, formed by incorporating Ni2+ into Mo-S lattice, shows plenty of substantial defects and active sites, which are favorable for the improvement of the overall electrochem. performances for both SIBs and HER.  When evaluated as the anode of SIBs, the NiMo3S4/CT electrode delivers a high specific capacity of ∼ 480 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.12 A g-1 and a high Coulombic efficiency of 100%.  Moreover, the NiMo3S4/CT electrode shows an excellent long-term cycling performance with a high reversible capacity of ∼ 302 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 0.48 A g-1, showing a high capacity retention of 73.9%.  Furthermore, as a HER catalyst, the NiMo3S4/CT hybrid nanostructure exhibits a low onset over-potential of 0.124 V, a small Tafel slope of 46.2 mV dec-1 as well as an excellent long-term stability, which are among the best values of current noble-metal-free electrocatalysts.  These results may open up a new route to introduce more active defect sites to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal sulfides by incorporation of metal elements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDiav-2t3oUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhG27qwr3XXJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpt12rs7s%253D&amp;md5=4008aad872988879aac64193a02178ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b06625"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Three-Dimensional Graphene Encapsulated with Hollow FeP@Carbon Nanocomposite as Outstanding Anode Material for Lithium Ion and Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xiujuan; Chen, Kai; Wang, Gang; Liu, Xiaojie; Wang, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
