        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have been extensively investigated owing to their high theor. capacities and relatively low intercalation potentials vs Li/Li+, but their practical applications have been hindered by low elec. cond. and dramatic vol. variation during cycling.  In this work, an interesting strategy for the rational design of graphene (GR) encapsulated with a hollow FeP@carbon nanocomposite (H-FeP@C@GR) via a combination of a hydrothermal route, a carbon-coating process, phosphidation treatment, and carbothermic reaction is reported.  The hollow FeP (H-FeP) nanospheres shelled with thin carbon layers are wonderfully incorporated into the GR matrix, interconnecting to form a three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical architecture.  Such a design offers distinct advantages for FeP-based anode materials for both lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, the 3D omnibearing conductive networks from the GR skeleton and outer coating carbon can provide an open freeway for electron/ion transport, promoting the electrode reaction kinetics.  In addn., the wrapping of an H-FeP nanosphere in a thin carbon layer enables the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on the carbon layer surface instead of on the individual H-FeP surface, preventing the continual re-forming of the SEI.  When used as anode materials for LIBs and SIBs, H-FeP@C@GR exhibited excellent electrochem. performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJNbfRlD70dbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhG27qwr3XXJA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhsbnP&amp;md5=60e49fafbda32645938e58b743ba2e5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA10272G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A facile sol-gel route to prepare functional graphene nanosheets anchored with homogeneous cobalt sulfide nanoparticles as superb sodium-ion anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Tingting; Ma, Yifan; Guo, Qiubo; Yang, Mei; Xia, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid metal sulfides with a graphene matrix is an efficient design to buffer the vol. expansion and fragmentation of vulnerable metal sulfides.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Insertion in Hollow Carbon Nanowires for Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yuliang; Xiao, Lifen; Sushko, Maria L.; Wang, Wei; Schwenzer, Birgit; Xiao, Jie; Nie, Zimin; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhengguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Ni3S2-PEDOT monolithic electrode for sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shang, Chaoqun; Dong, Shanmu; Zhang, Shengliang; Hu, Pu; Zhang, Chuanjian; Cui, Guanglei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochemistry Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24-27</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Ni3S2 attracts much attention for sodium batteries owing to its natural abundance, low cost, and high theor. capacity.  However, poor cond. of Ni3S2 and large vol. expansion hamper its potential application.  We describe a facile strategy to construct monolithic Ni3S2-Poly(3,4-ethylenedioxythiophene) (PEDOT) electrodes with stable electrochem. performance for sodium batteries.  Ni3S2 is directly grown on Ni foam substrate with superior electron transport efficiency.  The PEDOT layer would efficiently protect the Ni3S2 from being wrecked by the severe vol. expansion during charge-discharge process.  The as-prepd. Ni3S2-PEDOT electrodes display stable cycling performance with a capacity of 280 mAh g- 1 after 30 cycles between 0.5 and 2 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPF8tvS8EquLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgnz1iY8eUGZQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFCnsbnI&amp;md5=067d3d8fc5d70231c167331d72d2a605</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.matlet.2017.11.061"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Acicular NiS-Ni derived from a low temperature sulfuration method as freestanding electrode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Qichang; Ni, Shibing; Tang, Jun; Li, Tao; Kang, Tao; Yang, Xuelin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">213</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Acicular NiS on Ni foam was prepd. via a low temp. sulfuration method, using Ni foam as raw material.  The as-prepd. NiS-Ni electrode exhibits superior electrochem. performance as free-standing anode for half-cell and full-cell Na-ion batteries.  At a specific current of 0.03 A/g, it delivers initial discharge and charge capacities of 1368.8 and 813.6 mAh/g, maintaining of 504.8 and 497.4 mAh/g after 50 cycles.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Synthesis and Assembly of Ni3S4 Nanorods for Enhanced Electrochemical Sodium-Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Deng, Jun; Gong, Qiufang; Ye, Hualin; Feng, Kun; Zhou, Junhua; Zha, Chenyang; Wu, Jinghua; Chen, Junmei; Zhong, Jun; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1829-1836</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Even though advocated as the potential low-cost alternatives to current lithium-ion technol., the practical viability of sodium-ion batteries remains illusive and depends on the development of high-performance electrode materials.  Very few candidates available at present can simultaneously meet the requirements on capacity, rate capability, and cycle life.  Herein, we report a high-temp. soln. method to prep. Ni3S4 nanorods with uniform sizes.  These colloidal nanorods readily self-assemble side by side and form microsized superstructures, which unfortunately negates the nanoscale feature of individual nanorods.  To this end, we further introduce two-dimensional graphene nanosheets as the spacer to interrupt nanorod self-assembly.  Resultant composite presents a marked advantage toward electrochem. storage of Na+ ions.  We demonstrate that in half-cells it exhibits large reversible specific capacity in excess of 600 mAh/g, high rate capability with &gt;300 mAh/g retained at 4 A/g, and great cycle life at different current rates.  This anode material can also be combined with the NASICON-type Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode in full cells to enable large capacity and good cyclability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo24C8mtWl5SrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgnz1iY8eUGZQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXit1Wiu7Y%253D&amp;md5=e705922a40d1ca9d5991f7408ec4bbe6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201501785"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure-designed synthesis of FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes as a high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Zhiming; Lu, Tianchi; Song, Taeseup; Yu, Xin-Yao; Lou, Xiong Wen; Paik, Ungyu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pyrite (FeS2) is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with a high theor. capacity of 894 mAh g-1.  However, its practical application is greatly hindered by the rapid capacity fading caused by the large vol. expansion upon sodiation.  Tuning the morphol. and structure at nanoscale and applying a higher cut-off voltage are essential to address this issue.  Here, a facile etching method coupled with a novel sulfidation-in-nanobox strategy is developed to synthesize unique FeS2@C yolk-shell nanoboxes.  The as-obtained FeS2@C nanoboxes reveal excellent sodium storage performance.  The remarkable electrochem. properties are attributed to the elaborate yolk-shell nanoarchitecture.  In particular, it delivers a high specific capacity of 511 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Furthermore, a high specific capacity of 403 mAh g-1 even at 5 A g-1 is delivered.  Most impressively, a stable capacity of 330 mAh g-1 can still be retained at 2 A g-1 even after 800 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvJjmhFrYQyrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5_hI47A6ktQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXptFamsL0%253D&amp;md5=36e009c64dd7a8c52d074bf74fb945a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b03920"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, L.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Chemically Coupled Antimony/Multilayer Graphene Hybrid as a High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Lingyun; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Du, Yichen; Li, Yafei; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted considerable attention as a promising alternative to Li-ion batteries owing to the natural abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for Na-ion batteries, Sb is a desirable candidate due to its high theor. capacity (660 mA h g-1).  Herein, an Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid, in which Sb is homogeneously anchored on multilayer graphene, is produced by a confined vapor deposition method.  The chem. bonding can realize robust and intimate contact between Sb and multilayer graphene, and the uniform distribution of Sb and the highly conductive and flexible multilayer graphene can not only improve Na ion diffusion and electronic transport but also stabilize the solid electrolyte interphase upon the large vol. changes of Sb during cycling.  Consequently, the Sb/multilayer graphene hybrid shows a high reversible Na storage capacity (452 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1), stable long-term cycling performance with 90% capacity retention after 200 cycles, and excellent rate capability (210 mA h g-1 under 5000 mA g-1).  This facile synthesis approach and unique nanostructure can potentially be extended to other alloy materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDfBd8kZiyFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5_hI47A6ktQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvVCjtb7K&amp;md5=2d783871704dc4fcc47474721f1b1ab3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE44004D"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-quality Prussian blue crystals as superior cathode materials for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">You, Ya; Wu, Xing-Long; Yin, Ya-Xia; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-quality Prussian blue crystals with a small no. of vacancies and a low water content are obtained by employing Na4Fe(CN)6 as the single iron-source precursor.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Prussian Blue@C Composite as an Ultrahigh-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery Cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jiang, Yinzhu; Yu, Shenglan; Wang, Baoqi; Li, Yong; Sun, Wenping; Lu, Yunhao; Yan, Mi; Song, Bin; Dou, Shixue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">26</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">29</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5315-5321</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable sodium ion batteries (SIBs) are surfacing as promising candidates for applications in large-scale energy-storage systems.  Prussian blue (PB) and its analogs (PBAs) have been considered as potential cathodes because of their rigid open framework and low-cost synthesis.  Nevertheless, PBAs suffer from inferior rate capability and poor cycling stability resulting from the low electronic cond. and deficiencies in the PBAs framework.  Herein, to understand the vacancy-impacted sodium storage and Na-insertion reaction kinetics, we report on an in-situ synthesized PB@C composite as a high-performance SIB cathode.  Perfectly shaped, nanosized PB cubes were grown directly on carbon chains, assuring fast charge transfer and Na-ion diffusion.  The existence of [Fe(CN)6] vacancies in the PB crystal is found to greatly degrade the electrochem. activity of the FeLS(C) redox couple via first-principles computation.  Superior reaction kinetics are demonstrated for the redox reactions of the FeHS(N) couple, which rely on the partial insertion of Na ions to enhance the electron conduction.  The synergistic effects of the structure and morphol. results in the PB@C composite achieving an unprecedented rate capability and outstanding cycling stability (77.5 mAh g-1 at 90 C, 90 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles at 20 C with 90% capacity retention).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo693UCkOhO2rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5_hI47A6ktQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xot1Khtbo%253D&amp;md5=f90bf6c154f4b4dbd6247e7e07f0de7c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta12036h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-crystal FeFe(CN)6 nanoparticles: a high capacity and high rate cathode for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xianyong; Deng, Wenwen; Qian, Jiangfeng; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10130-10134</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prussian blue analogs are actively explored as low cost and high capacity cathodes for Na ion batteries; however, their applications are hindered by low capacity use and poor cyclability of these compds.  This problem can be solved by controlling the purity and crystallinity of the Prussian blue lattices.  As a model compd., single-crystal FeIIIFeIII(CN)6 nanoparticles are synthesized and found to have a sufficiently high capacity of 120 mA-h g-1, an exceptional rate capability at 20 C and superior cyclability with 87% capacity retention over 500 cycles, showing great promise for Na ion battery applications.  More significantly, these results provide a new insight into the intercalation chem. of Prussian blue analogs and open new perspectives to develop Na storage cathodes for widespread applications of elec. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcqkhMgh8BhrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljfVfOyiOmjYg"> &gt;&gt;             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This article proposes a strategy by designing a sandwich-like nanocomposite to overcome the disadvantages of the non-graphitized carbon materials.  This article summarizes that the developed a facile ionothermal method to synthesize sandwich-like hierarchically porous carbon/graphene composite, in which hierarchical porous carbon facilitates Na+ insertion and graphene guarantees the high electronic cond. for electrons supply.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrul7DVrUFn6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgkVpv0jpGQsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpt1Wjurk%253D&amp;md5=3dec7b7bfc133e4038c2ad0de8f47e12</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7929"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.                         rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGrV7K8Tq5mLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgkVpv0jpGQsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtF2lurzK&amp;md5=99303fd99ef59044874690750282067a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bommier, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRqzaoLtXoUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b15757"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two multifunctional metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) with the same coordination mode, [Co(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Co(L) MOF"] and [Cd(L)(H2O)]n·2nH2O [defined as "Cd(L) MOF"] (L = 5-aminoisophthalic acid) have been fabricated via a simple and versatile scalable solvothermal approach at 85 °C for 24 h.  The relationship between the structure of the electrode materials (esp. the coordination water and different metal ions) and the electrochem. properties of MOFs have been investigated for the first time.  And then the possible electrochem. mechanisms of the electrodes have been studied and proposed.  In addn., MOFs/RGO hybrid materials were prepd. via ball milling, which demonstrated better electrochem. performances than those of individual Co(L) MOF and Cd(L) MOF.  For example, when Co(L) MOF/RGO was applied as anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), it retained 206 mA h g-1 after 330 cycles at 500 mA g-1 and 1185 mA h g-1 could be obtained after 50 cycles at 100 mA g-1 for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  The high-discharge capacity, excellent cyclic stability combined with the facile synthesis procedure enable Co(L) MOF- and Cd(L) MOF-based materials to be prospective anode materials for SIBs and LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrYWKsq_6KCqrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRqzaoLtXoUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitFCntr4%253D&amp;md5=91879f6af546dcca6f04a7843c7d36f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201700606"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Spray-drying and the nanoscale Kirkendall diffusion process are used to prep. nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/reduced graphene oxide (rGO) composite powders with excellent Na-ion storage properties.  Metallic Ni nanopowder-decorated rGO powders, formed as intermediate products, are transformed into composite powders of nickel sulfide hollow nanospheres/rGO with mixed crystal structures of Ni3S2 and Ni9S8 phases by the sulfidation process under H2S gas.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox-active org. polymers are promising cathode electrodes owing to the advantages of open and flexible frame-works, renewability and environmental friendliness.  Sodium salt of poly(2, 5-dihydroxy-p-benzoquinonyl sulfide)/RGO (Na2PDHBQS/RGO) composite has been fabricated via a convenient route and applied as a high performance and stable cathode for sodium ion batteries.  The Na2PDHBQS/RGO was investigated in ether-based electrolyte, which demonstrated better electrochem. performances (228, 214, 203, 193, 172, and 147 mAh g-1 at 0.1, 0.2, 0.4, 0.8, 2 and 4C, resp.) than that in traditional ester-based ones.  The high specific capacity, excellent cycle stability and reversibility of Na2PDHBQS/RGO may be attributed to the special porous structure, enhanced electronic cond. by the introduction of RGO and fast sodium ion and electron diffusion rate in ether-based electrolyte.  In addn., the Na2PDHBQS/RGO cathode has been assembled with disodium terephthalate (Na2TP) anode to compose a full cell for the first time, which presents an initial reversible capacity of 210 mAh g-1 at 0.1C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqodbe4TVGTOrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljRqzaoLtXoUw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslSltbs%253D&amp;md5=0e1ba2594da5338f1f7748ccebbd2af7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref10" class="rightTabRefNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.01.005"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Y.                         rightTab-cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Supported Nanotube Arrays of Sulfur-Doped TiO2 Enabling Ultrastable and Robust Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ni, Jiangfeng; Fu, Shidong; Wu, Chao; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan; Li, Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We, for the 1st time, combine the unique nanotubular architecture with high cond. by engineering self-supported nanotube arrays of S-doped TiO2 (S-TiO2).  Such doping by isovalent substitution can be helpful owing to either elastic effect or, at high enough concn., to variation of materials const. (e.g., bandgap).  S-doped TiO2 materials have been reported and characterized, yet never used as electrodes for Na-based battery behaviors.  The increase of electronic cond. could be predominately ascribed to structure affects rather than proper doping, as shown by the strong effect on the band gap.  An addnl. possibility is the introduction of an anionic deficiency (anion vacancies compensated by electron due to prepn.).  Note the deoxygenation effect of S treatment, an aliovalent effect as, e.g., achieved by donor doping TiO2, may be excluded here.  The S-TiO2 nanotube array features intrinsic merits for Na storage.  First, the self-supported nanotube array can be directly adapted for electrode without using binder and C additive.  Second, the ordered nanotube architecture exhibits large interface and channels for transfer of Na ion during cycling.  Third, the S doping drastically boosts the electron movement within the nanotubes.  Consequently, the S-TiO2 nanotubes enable superior Na storage in terms of high capacity (320 mAh/g), ultrastable cycling (91% retention over 4400 cycles), and robust rate capability (167 mAh/g at 3.35 A/g).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrObwc1x3fRibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7DE1q7ZyFYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1ektbc%253D&amp;md5=cf8583f1f9e0593bbc7f6af9a5227e30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1039/C3EE42944J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination. Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg7DE1q7ZyFYQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel disulfide-graphene nanosheets (NiS2-GNS) composites were successfully synthesized via a simple and mild hydrothermal method.  It was revealed by SEM and transmission electron microscopy images that the spherical NiS2 nanoparticles with a diam. of 200-300 nm were uniformly dispersed on graphene nanosheets.  Na+ electrochem. storage properties including cycling performance and high-rate capability of NiS2-GNS composites were investigated, demonstrating a superior reversible capacity of 407 mAh g-1 with the capacity retention of 77% over 200 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal sulfides have been treated as promising materials for lithium-ion battery, and recently more and more attention has been paid to its applications in sodium-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering inherent large structural deterioration of conversion-type anode materials during repeated sodiation/desodiation process, the ingenious integration of both nanostructure engineering and chem. hybridization is highly desirable and challenging.  Here, ultrafine CoS nanoparticles embedded in porous carbon nanorods (denoted as 7-CoS/C) were facilely fabricated via simultaneous in-situ carbonization and sulfidation of Co-metal org. frameworks (Co-MOF) and have been applied as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Benefiting from the advantageous embedding architecture between the nanoparticles and porous nanorods, the 7-CoS/C delivers long-term cycling stability (542 mAh g-1 after 2000 cycles with a capacity retention of 91.4% at 1 A g-1) and excellent rate performance (discharge capacities of 510 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 and 356 mAh g-1 even at 40 A g-1), which is proved to be characterized of partial pseudocapacitive behaviors during the sodiation/desodiation process.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for energy storage due to the abundance of sodium, esp. for grid distribution systems.  The practical implementation of SIBs, however, is severely hindered by their low energy d. and poor cycling stability due to the poor electrochem. performance of the existing electrodes.  Here, to achieve high-capacity and durable sodium storage with good rate capability, hierarchical hollow NiS spheres with porous shells composed of nanoparticles are designed and synthesized by tuning the reaction parameters.  The formation mechanism of this unique structure is systematically investigated, which is clearly revealed to be Ostwald ripening mechanism on the basis of the time-dependent morphol. evolution.  The hierarchical hollow structure provides sufficient electrode/electrolyte contact, shortened Na+ diffusion pathways, and high strain-tolerance capability.  The hollow NiS spheres deliver high reversible capacity (683.8 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capability (337.4 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1), and good cycling stability (499.9 mAh g-1 with 73% retention after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqILcValYXCmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9ywaCnLS9bg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhsVymtrbN&amp;md5=df1523f34e777d5f61481d30ef557f22</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref20" class="rightTabRefNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit20" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2015.10.064"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is desirable to develop electrode materials for advanced rechargeable batteries with low cost, long life, and high-rate capability.  Pyrite FeS2, as an easily obtained natural mineral, has been already commercialized in primary lithium batteries, but encountered problems in rechargeable batteries with carbonate-based electrolytes due to the limited cycle life caused by the conversion-type reaction (FeS2 + 4M → Fe + 2M2S (M = Li or Na)).  Herein, we demonstrate that FeS2 microspheres can be applied in room-temp. rechargeable sodium batteries with only the intercalation reaction by simultaneously selecting a compatible NaSO3CF3/diglyme electrolyte and tuning the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V.  A surprisingly high-rate capability (170 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1) and unprecedented long-term cyclability (∼90% capacity retention for 20 000 cycles) has been obtained.  We suggest that a stable elec. conductive layer-structured NaxFeS2 was formed during cycling, which enables the highly reversible sodium intercalation and deintercalation.  Moreover, 18650-type sodium batteries were constructed exhibiting a high capacity of ∼4200 mA h (corresponding to 126 W h kg-1 and 382 W h L-1) and a capacity retention of 97% after an initial 200 cycles at 4 A during charge-discharge.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrocatalytic activity of transition metal sulfides is strongly correlated with the active edge sites and cond. of the catalysts.  Here we developed a hybrid nanowire structure consisting of NiS2-MoS2 interlaced nanoflakes by the thermal conversion of nickel molybdate (NiMoO4) nanowire precursors.  The obtained NiS2-MoS2 interlaced nanoflakes have sub-200 nm sizes with abundant active edge sites and defects, as well as synergistic nanoscale interfaces between NiS2 and MoS2 throughout the whole structure.  The hetero-nanowires exhibit superior hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) catalytic activity including a low onset potential of 76 mV and a small Tafel slope of 70 mV dec-1 in a 1 M KOH aq. soln., which substantially exceeds those of most of the metal sulfide HER catalysts including individual NiS2 and MoS2 nanostructures in basic solns.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBzNHqSQIEFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9ywaCnLS9bg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1WmtbfE&amp;md5=8222f389eb32031ad1089919c0d77a96</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1007/s10008-017-3600-9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.                         rightTab-cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of NiS/carbon composites as anodes for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jinkai; Cao, Daxian; Yang, Guidong; Yang, Yaodong; Wang, Hongkang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Electrochemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We demonstrate a general solid-state synthesis of nickel sulfide (NiS) and carbon-based composites (NiS/C) via simple thermal decompn. of nickel dibutyldithiocarbamate (C18H36N2NiS4) under ambient atm., which can be applied to various carbon-based materials such as 2D graphene nanosheets (GNSs), 1D carbon nanotubes (CNTs), and 0D carbon black (CB).  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the as-prepd. NiS/C composites demonstrate excellent sodium storage properties including superior cycle stability and rate capability, delivering reversible capacities of 483 (for NiS/GNSs), 394 (for NiS/CNTs), and 413 mAh/g (for NiS/CB) at a c.d. of 200 mA/g after 100 cycles, resp., which are much higher than that of the bare NiS counterpart (136 mAh/g at 200 mA/g after 100 cycles).  Moreover, reversible capacities of 372 mAh/g for NiS/GNSs, 331 mAh/g for NiS/CNTs, and 317 mAh/g for NiS/CB are realized at a high rate of 2 A/g.  The excellent electrochem. performance can be attributed to the introduction of the carbon-based materials, which not only serve as efficient buffering matrixes to tolerate the vol. changes of NiS upon sodiation/desodiation but also improve the electrode cond.  More importantly, this work provides a straightforward and general synthetic approach for designing various NiS/C composites as high-performance anodes for electrochem. energy storage.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Prepn. of two-dimensional (2D) graphene-like materials is currently an emerging field in materials science since the discovery of single-atom-thick graphene prepd. by mech. cleavage.  In this work, we proposed a new method to prep. 2D NiS, where reduced graphene oxide (rGO) was found to induce the recrystn. of NiS from nanorods to nanosheets in a hydrothermal process.  The process and mechanism of recrystn. have been clarified by various characterization techniques, including SEM, transmission electron microscopy (TEM), energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) mapping, and XPS.  The characterization of ex situ NiS/rGO products by SEM and EDS mapping indicates that the recrystn. of NiS from nanorods to nanosheets is realized actually through an exfoliation process, while the characterization of in situ NiS/rGO products by SEM, TEM, and EDS mapping reveals the exfoliation process.  The XPS result demonstrates that hydrothermally assisted chem. bonding occurs between NiS and rGO, which induces the exfoliation of NiS nanorods into nanosheets.  The obtained NiS/rGO composite shows promising Na-storage properties.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqY5KHERzDl-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyGyfB0q1fFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXksF2rtb0%253D&amp;md5=e7ec208b87afc61d8e4703751d36bc98</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acscatal.5b00154"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ganesan, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sanetuntikul, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shanmugam, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cobalt Sulfide Nanoparticles Grown on Nitrogen and Sulfur Codoped Graphene Oxide: An Efficient Electrocatalyst for Oxygen Reduction and Evolution Reactions</span>. <i>ACS Catal.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3625</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3637</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. oxygen evolution and redn. reactions have received great attention due to their importance in several key technologies such as fuel cells, electrolyzers, and metal-air batteries.  Here, we present a simple approach to the prepn. of cobalt sulfide nanoparticles in situ grown on a nitrogen- and sulfur-codoped graphene oxide surface.  The particle size and phase were controlled by changing the treatment temp.  Cobalt sulfide nanoparticles dispersed on graphene oxide hybrids were successfully prepd. by a solid-state thermolysis approach at different temps. (400, 500, and 600°) using cobalt-thiourea complex and graphene oxide.  X-ray diffraction studies revealed that hybrids prepd. at 400 and 500 °C result in pure CoS2 phase, whereas the hybrid prepd. at 600 °C exhibits Co9S8 phase.  XPS studies revealed that nitrogen and sulfur simultaneously codoped on the graphene oxide surface, and these sites act to anchor the CoS2 nanoparticles strongly on the GO surface.  The strong coupling between CoS2 and N,S-GO was reflected in the improvement of the oxygen electrode potential.  CoS2(400)/N,S-GO showed an outstanding oxygen electrode activity with a potential of about 0.82 V against a reversible hydrogen electrode in alk. medium, which is far better than the performance of precious catalysts such as Pt/C (1.16 V), Ru/C (1.01 V), and Ir/C (0.92 V).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1sLK9FiN1f7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyGyfB0q1fFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXnsFOgtbY%253D&amp;md5=ef218509d1975cd741dfe4878d7c84cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.04.011"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Cobalt sulfides are attractive as intriguing candidates for anodes in SIBs and LIBs owing to their unique chem. and phys. properties.  In this study, a precursor of Co1-xS with a uniform and hollow nanospherical architecture is obtained with a high yield via a mild solvothermal method in the presence of 2-methylimidazole at first.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal phosphides have been extensively investigated owing to their high theor. capacities and relatively low intercalation potentials vs Li/Li+, but their practical applications have been hindered by low elec. cond. and dramatic vol. variation during cycling.  In this work, an interesting strategy for the rational design of graphene (GR) encapsulated with a hollow FeP@carbon nanocomposite (H-FeP@C@GR) via a combination of a hydrothermal route, a carbon-coating process, phosphidation treatment, and carbothermic reaction is reported.  The hollow FeP (H-FeP) nanospheres shelled with thin carbon layers are wonderfully incorporated into the GR matrix, interconnecting to form a three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical architecture.  Such a design offers distinct advantages for FeP-based anode materials for both lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  For example, the 3D omnibearing conductive networks from the GR skeleton and outer coating carbon can provide an open freeway for electron/ion transport, promoting the electrode reaction kinetics.  In addn., the wrapping of an H-FeP nanosphere in a thin carbon layer enables the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) on the carbon layer surface instead of on the individual H-FeP surface, preventing the continual re-forming of the SEI.  When used as anode materials for LIBs and SIBs, H-FeP@C@GR exhibited excellent electrochem. performances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoJNbfRlD70dbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyGyfB0q1fFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhs1yhsbnP&amp;md5=60e49fafbda32645938e58b743ba2e5d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00201G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A binary Ni/Co metal org. framework (Ni-Co-MOF) with a hollow-sphere structure that is decorated with cone-shaped protrusions was prepd. via a facile solvothermal reaction.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nickel sulfide, a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), has drawn a lot of attention due to its natural abundance, low cost, rich types and high theor. specific capacity (Ni3S2: 446, NiS: 591 and NiS2: 879 mA h g-1).  However, the huge vol. change-induced severe electrode pulverization results in the low specific capacity and poor cycling stability of nickel sulfide electrodes.  Herein, in this paper, we developed a metal-org. framework (MOF) strategy to prep. pomegranate-like clusters with small NiS2 nanoparticles anchored on nitrogen doped porous graphitic carbon networks (NiS2/NC) via successive carbonization and sulfidation.  When evaluated as an anode for SIBs, the as-prepd. NiS2/NC hybrid exhibited a high reversible capacity of 505.7 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g-1, excellent rate capability (294.4 mA h g-1 at 3 A g-1) and robust cycling stability with a capacity of 356.2 mA h g-1 after 300 cycles at 0.5 A g-1, which outperforms most of the nickel sulfide based electrodes reported so far.  The excellent cycling performance and rate capability for SIBs can be attributed to the unique structure inherited from nickel based MOFs, in situ fabrication strategy, high capacity of NiS2, and conductive and buffering features of the nitrogen-doped graphitic carbon networks, demonstrating the great potential of the as-prepd. NiS2/NC hybrid for high-performance SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqyF8tMrvq_a7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhyGyfB0q1fFQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXksFagsLc%253D&amp;md5=b1af16a601c2a22cf423f7a9c4691f0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201800054"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhai, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A hierarchical hybrid nanostructure composed of NiMo3S4 nanosheet arrays with abundant exposed edges on flexible carbon textiles (denoted as NiMo3S4/CTs) has been designed and synthesized for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and electrocatalytic hydrogen evolution reaction (HER).  The novel NiMo3S4 nanostructure, formed by incorporating Ni2+ into Mo-S lattice, shows plenty of substantial defects and active sites, which are favorable for the improvement of the overall electrochem. performances for both SIBs and HER.  When evaluated as the anode of SIBs, the NiMo3S4/CT electrode delivers a high specific capacity of ∼ 480 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.12 A g-1 and a high Coulombic efficiency of 100%.  Moreover, the NiMo3S4/CT electrode shows an excellent long-term cycling performance with a high reversible capacity of ∼ 302 mA h g-1 after 1000 cycles at 0.48 A g-1, showing a high capacity retention of 73.9%.  Furthermore, as a HER catalyst, the NiMo3S4/CT hybrid nanostructure exhibits a low onset over-potential of 0.124 V, a small Tafel slope of 46.2 mV dec-1 as well as an excellent long-term stability, which are among the best values of current noble-metal-free electrocatalysts.  These results may open up a new route to introduce more active defect sites to enhance the electrochem. performance of metal sulfides by incorporation of metal elements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDiav-2t3oUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liQiVTodFzdCQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXpt12rs7s%253D&amp;md5=4008aad872988879aac64193a02178ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref37" class="rightTabRefNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.7b06625"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.
